	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Good Friday</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the holiday. For the peace deal, see <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Good Friday (disambiguation)">Good Friday (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

services, <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fasting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almsgiving" class="mw-redirect" title="Almsgiving">almsgiving</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date</th><td>The Friday (Western)</li><li>April 30 (Eastern)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Frequency</th><td>Annual</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Related&#160;to</th><td><a href="/wiki/Passover" href="/wiki/Septuagesima" title="Septuagesima">Septuagesima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quinquagesima" title="Quinquagesima">Quinquagesima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shrove_Tuesday" title="Shrove Tuesday">Shrove Tuesday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ash_Wednesday" title="Ash Wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lent" title="Lent">Lent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_Sunday" title="Palm Sunday">Palm Sunday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Divine_Mercy_Sunday" title="Divine Mercy Sunday">Divine Mercy Sunday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascension of Jesus Christ">Ascension</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">Pentecost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whit_Monday" title="Whit Monday">Whit Monday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Sunday" title="Trinity Sunday">Trinity Sunday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_(feast)" title="Corpus Christi (feast)">Corpus Christi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_the_Sacred_Heart" title="Feast of the Sacred Heart">Feast of the Sacred Heart</a> which follow it. It is related to the Feast of the <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_of_the_Holy_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Exaltation of the Holy Cross">Exaltation of the Holy Cross</a>, which focuses on the benefits, graces, and merits of the Cross, rather than Jesus's death.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Good Friday</b> is a Christian <a href="/wiki/Holiday" title="Holiday">holiday</a> commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">crucifixion of Jesus</a> and his death at <a href="/wiki/Calvary" title="Calvary">Calvary</a>. It is observed during <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">Holy Week</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Paschal_Triduum" title="Paschal Triduum">Paschal Triduum</a> on the Friday preceding <a href="/wiki/Easter_Sunday" class="mw-redirect" title="Easter Sunday">Easter Sunday</a>, and may coincide with the Jewish observance of <a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">Passover</a>. It is also known as <b>Holy Friday</b>, <b>Great Friday</b>, and <b>Black Friday</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Members of many <a href="/wiki/Christian_denominations" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian denominations">Christian denominations</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>, Protestant, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a>  traditions, observe Good Friday with <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fasting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Church_service" title="Church service">church services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RipleyDana1883_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RipleyDana1883-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pfatteicher1990_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pfatteicher1990-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JacobsHaas1899_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JacobsHaas1899-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Computus" title="Computus">date of Good Friday</a> varies from one year to the next on both the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian</a> calendars. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a> disagree over the computation of the date of Easter and therefore of Good Friday. Good Friday is a widely instituted <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">legal holiday</a> around the world, including in most <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western countries</a> and <a href="#United_States">12 U.S. states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Some countries, such as Germany, have laws prohibiting certain acts, such as dancing and horse racing, that are seen as profaning the solemn nature of the day.<sup id="cite_ref-Petre_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petre-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stevens_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stevens-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A common <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a> claims "Good Friday" is a corruption of "God Friday", as was the case with the contraction <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/goodbye" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:goodbye">goodbye</a>. The term in fact comes from the sense "pious, holy" of the word <i>good</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Oxford English Dictionary</i> also gives other examples with the sense "of a day or season observed as holy by the church" as an archaic sense of <i>good</i> (<i>good</i>, adj. 8c) as in <i>good tide</i> meaning "Christmas" or "Shrove Tuesday", and <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Wednesday" class="mw-redirect" title="Good Wednesday">Good Wednesday</a></i> meaning the Wednesday in Holy Week.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Catechism" title="Baltimore Catechism">Baltimore Catechism</a></i> states that this day is called "Good Friday" because <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Christianity" title="Jesus in Christianity">Jesus</a> "showed his great love for man, and purchased for him every blessing".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC2014_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2014-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_languages">Other languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Other languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Dutch Good Friday is known as <i>Goede Vrijdag</i>, in Frisian as <i>Goedfreed</i>. In German-speaking countries, Good Friday is generally referred to as <i>Karfreitag</i> (<i>Kar</i> from <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> <i>kara</i>â "bewail", "grieve"â "mourn", Freitag for "Friday"): Mourning Friday. The <i>Kar</i> prefix is a <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognate</a> of the English word "care" in the sense of cares and woes; it meant mourning. The day is also known as <i>Stiller Freitag</i> ("Silent Friday") and <i>Hoher Freitag</i> ("High Friday, Holy Friday"). In the Nordic countries it is called "The Long Friday". In Greek, Polish and Hungarian, Good Friday is generally referred to as <i>Great Friday</i> (<i>ÎÎµÎ³Î¬Î»Î· Î Î±ÏÎ±ÏÎºÎµÏÎ®</i>, <i>Wielki PiÄtek</i>, <i>NagypÃ©ntek</i>). In Bulgarian, Good Friday is called either <i>ÐÐµÐ»Ð¸ÐºÐ¸ Ð¿ÐµÑÑÐº</i> â  <i>Great Friday</i>, or, more commonly, <i>Ð Ð°Ð·Ð¿ÐµÑÐ¸ Ð¿ÐµÑÑÐº</i> (approximate pronunciation 'razpeti petak') which literally translates to "Crucified Friday". In French, Good Friday is referred to as <i>Vendredi saint</i> ("Holy Friday").
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biblical_accounts">Biblical accounts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Biblical accounts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Passion_(Christianity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Passion (Christianity)">Passion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Crucifixion of Jesus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sayings_of_Jesus_on_the_cross" title="Sayings of Jesus on the cross">Sayings of Jesus on the cross</a></div>

</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
<small><small><b>Portals: </b><a href="/wiki/File:P_christianity.svg" class="image"><img alt="P christianity.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/16px-P_christianity.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/24px-P_christianity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/32px-P_christianity.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="360" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Christianity" title="Portal:Christianity">Christianity</a> <a href="/wiki/File:Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg/16px-Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="16" height="10" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg/24px-Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg/32px-Bible.malmesbury.arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1993" data-file-height="1300" /></a>  <a href="/wiki/Portal:Bible" title="Portal:Bible">Bible</a></small></small></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Death_of_Jesus" title="Template:Death of Jesus"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Death_of_Jesus" title="Template talk:Death of Jesus"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Death_of_Jesus&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>According to the accounts in the Gospels, the royal soldiers, guided by Jesus' disciple <a href="/wiki/Judas_Iscariot" title="Judas Iscariot">Judas Iscariot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrest_of_Jesus" title="Arrest of Jesus">arrested</a> Jesus in the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Gethsemane" class="mw-redirect" title="Garden of Gethsemane">Garden of Gethsemane</a>. Judas received money (<a href="/wiki/30_pieces_of_silver" class="mw-redirect" title="30 pieces of silver">30 pieces of silver</a>) (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#26:14" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 26:14â16</a>) for <a href="/wiki/Bargain_of_Judas" title="Bargain of Judas">betraying Jesus</a> and told the guards that whomever <a href="/wiki/Kiss_of_Judas" title="Kiss of Judas">he kisses</a> is the one they are to arrest. Following his arrest, Jesus was taken to the house of <a href="/wiki/Annas" title="Annas">Annas</a>, the father-in-law of the <a href="/wiki/Cohen_Gadol" class="mw-redirect" title="Cohen Gadol">high priest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caiaphas" title="Caiaphas">Caiaphas</a>. There he was interrogated with little result and sent bound to Caiaphas the high priest where the <a href="/wiki/Sanhedrin" title="Sanhedrin">Sanhedrin</a> had assembled (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#18:1" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 18:1â24</a>).
</p><p>Conflicting testimony against Jesus was brought forth by many witnesses, to which Jesus answered nothing. Finally the high priest adjured Jesus to respond under solemn oath, saying "I adjure you, by the Living God, to tell us, are you the Anointed One, the Son of God?" Jesus testified ambiguously, "You have said it, and in time you will see the Son of Man seated at the right hand of the Almighty, coming on the clouds of Heaven." The high priest condemned Jesus for <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy" title="Blasphemy">blasphemy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sanhedrin_Trial_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanhedrin Trial of Jesus">Sanhedrin concurred with a sentence of death</a> (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#26:57" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 26:57â66</a>). Peter, waiting in the courtyard, also <a href="/wiki/Denial_of_Peter" title="Denial of Peter">denied Jesus</a> three times to bystanders while the interrogations were proceeding just as Jesus had predicted.
</p><p>In the morning, the whole assembly brought Jesus to the Roman governor <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate" title="Pontius Pilate">Pontius Pilate</a> under charges of subverting the nation, opposing taxes to Caesar, and making himself a king (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Luke#23:1" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Luke">Luke 23:1â2</a>). Pilate authorized the Jewish leaders to judge Jesus according to their own law and execute sentencing; however, the Jewish leaders replied that they were not allowed by the Romans to carry out a sentence of death (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#18:31" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 18:31</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pilate%27s_court" title="Pilate&#39;s court">Pilate questioned</a> Jesus and told the assembly that there was no basis for sentencing. Upon learning that Jesus was from Galilee, Pilate referred the case to the ruler of <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herod_Antipas" title="Herod Antipas">King Herod</a>, who was in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">Passover</a> Feast. <a href="/wiki/Jesus_at_Herod%27s_court" title="Jesus at Herod&#39;s court">Herod questioned</a> Jesus but received no answer; Herod sent Jesus back to Pilate. Pilate told the assembly that neither he nor Herod found Jesus to be guilty; Pilate resolved to have Jesus whipped and released (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Luke#23:3" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Luke">Luke 23:3â16</a>). Under the guidance of the chief priests, the crowd asked for <a href="/wiki/Barabbas" title="Barabbas">Barabbas</a>, who had been imprisoned for committing murder during an insurrection. Pilate asked what they would have him do with Jesus, and they demanded, "Crucify him" (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Mark#15:6" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Mark">Mark 15:6â14</a>). <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate%27s_wife" title="Pontius Pilate&#39;s wife">Pilate's wife</a> had seen Jesus in a dream earlier that day, and she forewarned Pilate to "have nothing to do with this righteous man" (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:19" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:19</a>). Pilate had Jesus <a href="/wiki/Flagellation_of_Christ" title="Flagellation of Christ">flogged</a> and then brought him out to the crowd to release him. The chief priests informed Pilate of a new charge, demanding Jesus be sentenced to death "because he claimed to be God's son." This possibility filled Pilate with fear, and he brought Jesus back inside the palace and demanded to know from where he came (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:1" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:1â9</a>).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_%281%29.jpg/220px-Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_%281%29.jpg/330px-Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_%281%29.jpg/440px-Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ecce_homo_by_Antonio_Ciseri_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Ciseri" title="Antonio Ciseri">Antonio Ciseri</a>'s depiction of <i><a href="/wiki/Ecce_Homo" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecce Homo">Ecce Homo</a></i> with Jesus and <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate" title="Pontius Pilate">Pontius Pilate</a>, 19th century</div></div></div>
<p>Coming before the crowd one last time, Pilate declared Jesus innocent and washed his own hands in water to show he had no part in this condemnation. Nevertheless, Pilate handed Jesus over to be crucified in order to forestall a riot (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:24" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:24â26</a>) and ultimately to keep his job. The sentence written was "Jesus of Nazareth, King of the Jews." Jesus carried his cross to the site of execution (assisted by <a href="/wiki/Simon_of_Cyrene" title="Simon of Cyrene">Simon of Cyrene</a>), called the "place of the Skull", or "<a href="/wiki/Golgotha" class="mw-redirect" title="Golgotha">Golgotha</a>" in Hebrew and in Latin "Calvary". There he was crucified along with two criminals (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:17" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:17â22</a>).
</p><p>Jesus agonized on the cross for six hours. During his last three hours on the cross, from noon to 3&#160;pm, <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_darkness" title="Crucifixion darkness">darkness fell over the whole land</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Jesus <a href="/wiki/Sayings_of_Jesus_on_the_cross" title="Sayings of Jesus on the cross">spoke from the cross</a>, quoting the messianic <a href="/wiki/Psalm_22" title="Psalm 22">Psalm 22</a>: "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?"
</p><p>With a loud cry, Jesus gave up his spirit. There was an earthquake, tombs broke open, and the curtain in the Temple was torn from top to bottom. The <a href="/wiki/Centurion" title="Centurion">centurion</a> on guard at the site of crucifixion declared, "Truly this was God's Son!" (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:45" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:45â54</a>)
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_of_Arimathea" title="Joseph of Arimathea">Joseph of Arimathea</a>, a member of the Sanhedrin and secret follower of Jesus, who had not consented to his condemnation, went to Pilate to request the body of Jesus (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Luke#23:50" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Luke">Luke 23:50â52</a>). Another secret follower of Jesus and member of the Sanhedrin named <a href="/wiki/Nicodemus" title="Nicodemus">Nicodemus</a> brought about a hundred-pound weight mixture of spices and helped wrap the body of Jesus (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:39" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:39â40</a>). Pilate asked confirmation from the centurion of whether Jesus was dead (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Mark#15:44" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Mark">Mark 15:44</a>). A soldier pierced the side of Jesus with a lance causing blood and water to flow out (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:34" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:34</a>), and the centurion informed Pilate that Jesus was dead (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Mark#15:45" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Mark">Mark 15:45</a>).
</p><p>Joseph of Arimathea took Jesus' body, wrapped it in a clean linen shroud, and placed it in his own new tomb that had been carved in the rock (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:59" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:59â60</a>) in a garden near the site of crucifixion. Nicodemus (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#3:1" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 3:1</a>) also brought 75 pounds of <a href="/wiki/Myrrh" title="Myrrh">myrrh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aloes" class="mw-redirect" title="Aloes">aloes</a>, and placed them in the linen with the body, in keeping with Jewish burial customs (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:39" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:39â40</a>). They rolled a large rock over the entrance of the tomb (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:60" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:60</a>). Then they returned home and rested, because <a href="/wiki/Shabbat" title="Shabbat">Shabbat</a> had begun at sunset (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Luke#23:54" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Luke">Luke 23:54â56</a>). Matt. 28:1 "After the Shabbat, at dawn on the first day of the week, Mary Magdalene and the other Mary went to look at the tomb". i.e. "After the Sabbath, at dawn on the first day of the week,...". "He is not here; he has risen, just as he said....". (Matt. 28:6)
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Eastern_and_Oriental_Orthodox_Christianity">In Eastern and Oriental Orthodox Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: In Eastern and Oriental Orthodox Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg/220px-Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg/330px-Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg/440px-Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crucifixion_by_Theophanes_the_Cretan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">Icon</a> of the Crucifixion, 16th century, by <a href="/wiki/Theophanes_the_Cretan" title="Theophanes the Cretan">Theophanes the Cretan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Stavronikita_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Stavronikita Monastery">Stavronikita Monastery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Athos" title="Mount Athos">Mount Athos</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Byzantine Christians (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Christians">Eastern Christians</a> who follow the <a href="/wiki/Rite_of_Constantinople" class="mw-redirect" title="Rite of Constantinople">Rite of Constantinople</a>: <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Greek Catholic Church">Greek-Catholics</a>) call this day "Great and Holy Friday", or simply "Great Friday".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Because the sacrifice of Jesus through his crucifixion is commemorated on this day, the <a href="/wiki/Divine_Liturgy" title="Divine Liturgy">Divine Liturgy</a> (the sacrifice of bread and wine) is never celebrated on Great Friday, except when this day coincides with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Feast" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Feast">Great Feast</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Annunciation" title="Annunciation">Annunciation</a>, which falls on the fixed date of 25 March (for those churches which follow the traditional <a href="/wiki/Julian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Calendar">Julian Calendar</a>, 25 March currently falls on 7 April of the modern <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregorian Calendar">Gregorian Calendar</a>). Also on Great Friday, the clergy no longer wear the purple or red that is customary throughout <a href="/wiki/Great_Lent" title="Great Lent">Great Lent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> but instead don <a href="/wiki/Black_vestments" class="mw-redirect" title="Black vestments">black vestments</a>. There is no "stripping of the altar" on <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">Holy and Great Thursday</a> as in the West; instead, all of the <a href="/wiki/Antipendia" class="mw-redirect" title="Antipendia">church hangings</a> are changed to black, and will remain so until the Divine Liturgy on <a href="/wiki/Great_Saturday" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Saturday">Great Saturday</a>.
</p><p>The faithful revisit the events of the day through public reading of specific <a href="/wiki/Psalms" title="Psalms">Psalms</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospels</a>, and singing <a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">hymns</a> about Christ's death. Rich visual imagery and symbolism as well as stirring hymnody are remarkable elements of these observances. In the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox theology">Orthodox understanding</a>, the events of <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">Holy Week</a> are not simply an annual commemoration of past events, but the faithful actually participate in the death and <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection of Jesus">resurrection of Jesus</a>.
</p>
<blockquote><p>Each hour of this day is the new suffering and the new effort of the expiatory suffering of the Savior. And the echo of this suffering is already heard in every word of our worship service â unique and incomparable both in the power of tenderness and feeling and in the depth of the boundless compassion for the suffering of the Savior. The Holy Church opens before the eyes of believers a full picture of the redeeming suffering of the Lord beginning with the bloody sweat in the Garden of Gethsemane up to the crucifixion on Golgotha. Taking us back through the past centuries in thought, the Holy Church brings us to the foot of the cross of Christ erected on Golgotha, and makes us present among the quivering spectators of all the torture of the Savior.<sup id="cite_ref-Bulg_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bulg-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Great and Holy Friday is observed as a strict <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fast</a>, also called the <a href="/wiki/Black_Fast" title="Black Fast">Black Fast</a>, and adult Byzantine Christians are expected to abstain from all food and drink the entire day to the extent that their health permits. "On this Holy day neither a meal is offered nor do we eat on this day of the crucifixion. If someone is unable or has become very old [or is] unable to fast, he may be given bread and water after sunset. In this way we come to the holy commandment of the Holy Apostles not to eat on Great Friday."<sup id="cite_ref-Bulg_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bulg-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Matins_of_Holy_and_Great_Friday">Matins of Holy and Great Friday</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Matins of Holy and Great Friday">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Byzantine Christian observance of Holy and Great Friday, which is formally known as <b>The Order of Holy and Saving Passion of our Lord Jesus Christ</b>, begins on Thursday night with the <i><b>Matins of the Twelve Passion Gospels</b></i>. Scattered throughout this <a href="/wiki/Matins" title="Matins">Matins</a> service are twelve readings from all four of the Gospels which recount the events of the <a href="/wiki/Passion_(Christianity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Passion (Christianity)">Passion</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Last_Supper" title="Last Supper">Last Supper</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion" title="Crucifixion">Crucifixion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Sepulchre" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Sepulchre">burial</a> of Jesus. Some churches have a candelabrum with twelve candles on it, and after each Gospel reading one of the candles is extinguished.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg/170px-Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg/255px-Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg/340px-Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2157" data-file-height="2996" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Agias_Triados_frescos_cross.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Good Friday cross from the <a href="/wiki/Katholikon" title="Katholikon">Catholicon</a> at Holy Trinity Monastery, <a href="/wiki/Meteora" title="Meteora">Meteora</a>, Greece</div></div></div>
<p>The first of these twelve readings <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#13:31" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 13:31â18:1</a> is the longest Gospel reading of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_liturgical_calendar" title="Eastern Orthodox liturgical calendar">liturgical year</a>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Concatenation" title="Concatenation">concatenation</a> from all <a href="/wiki/Four_Gospels" class="mw-redirect" title="Four Gospels">four Gospels</a>. Just before the sixth Gospel reading, which recounts Jesus being nailed to the cross, a large <a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">cross</a> is carried out of the sanctuary by the priest, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Incense" title="Incense">incense</a> and candles, and is placed in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> (where the congregation gathers)<i>SÄmeron KremÄtai EpÃ­ XÃ½lou</i>:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Today He who hung the earth upon the waters is hung upon the Cross <i>(three times)</i>.<br />He who is King of the angels is arrayed in a crown of thorns.<br />He who wraps the Heavens in clouds is wrapped in the purple of mockery. <br />He who in Jordan set Adam free receives blows upon His face.<br />The Bridegroom of the Church is transfixed with nails. <br />The Son of the Virgin is pierced with a spear.<br />We venerate Thy Passion, O Christ <i>(three times)</i>.<br />Show us also Thy glorious Resurrection.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The readings are:
</p>
<ol><li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#13:31" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 13:31â18:1</a> â Christ's last sermon, Jesus prays for the <a href="/wiki/Apostles" title="Apostles">apostles</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#18:1" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 18:1â28</a> â The agony in the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Gethsemane" class="mw-redirect" title="Garden of Gethsemane">garden</a>, the mockery and denial of Christ.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#26:57" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 26:57â75</a> â The mockery of Christ, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Peter</a> denies Christ.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#18:28" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 18:28â19:16</a> â <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate" title="Pontius Pilate">Pilate</a> questions Jesus; Jesus is condemned; Jesus is mocked by the Romans.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:3" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:3â32</a> â <a href="/wiki/Judas" class="mw-redirect" title="Judas">Judas</a> commits suicide; Jesus is condemned; Jesus mocked by the Romans; <a href="/wiki/Simon_of_Cyrene" title="Simon of Cyrene">Simon of Cyrene</a> compelled to carry the cross.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Mark#15:16" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Mark">Mark 15:16â32</a> â <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Jesus dies</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:33" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:33â54</a> â <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Jesus dies</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Luke#23:32" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Luke">Luke 23:32â49</a> â <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Jesus dies</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:25" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:25â37</a> â <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Jesus dies</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Mark#15:43" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Mark">Mark 15:43â47</a> â <a href="/wiki/Joseph_of_Arimathea" title="Joseph of Arimathea">Joseph of Arimathea</a> buries Christ.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#19:38" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 19:38â42</a> â <a href="/wiki/Joseph_of_Arimathea" title="Joseph of Arimathea">Joseph of Arimathea</a> buries Christ.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Matthew#27:62" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Matthew">Matthew 27:62â66</a> â The Jews set a guard.</li></ol>
<p>During the service, all come forward to kiss the feet of Christ on the cross. After the <a href="/wiki/Canon_(hymnography)" title="Canon (hymnography)">Canon</a>, a brief, moving hymn, <i>The Wise Thief</i> is chanted by singers who stand at the foot of the cross in the center of the nave. The service does not end with the <a href="/wiki/First_Hour" class="mw-redirect" title="First Hour">First Hour</a>, as usual, but with a special <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(liturgy)" title="Dismissal (liturgy)">dismissal</a> by the priest:
</p>
<blockquote><p>May Christ our true God, Who for the salvation of the world endured spitting, and scourging, and buffeting, and the Cross, and death, through the intercessions of His <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">most pure Mother</a>, of our holy and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Fathers">God-bearing fathers</a>, and of all the <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saints</a>, have mercy on us and save us, for He is good and the Lover of mankind.</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Hours">Royal Hours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Royal Hours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation,_Toronto,_2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation%2C_Toronto%2C_2014.JPG/220px-Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation%2C_Toronto%2C_2014.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation%2C_Toronto%2C_2014.JPG/330px-Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation%2C_Toronto%2C_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation%2C_Toronto%2C_2014.JPG/440px-Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation%2C_Toronto%2C_2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3611" data-file-height="2708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Service_of_the_Royal_Hours_-_Great_Friday_--_Annunciation,_Toronto,_2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vigil during the Service of the Royal Hours.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hours" title="Royal Hours">Royal Hours</a></div>
<p>The next day, in the forenoon on Friday, all gather again to pray the <i><b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VRSgOFbH-fQ">Royal Hours</a></b></i>, a special expanded celebration of the <a href="/wiki/Little_Hours" title="Little Hours">Little Hours</a> (including the First Hour, <a href="/wiki/Third_Hour" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Hour">Third Hour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sext" title="Sext">Sixth Hour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Hour" class="mw-redirect" title="Ninth Hour">Ninth Hour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typica" title="Typica">Typica</a>) with the addition of scripture readings (<a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epistle" title="Epistle">Epistle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospel</a>) and hymns about the Crucifixion at each of the Hours (some of the material from the previous night is repeated). This is somewhat more festive in character, and derives its name of "Royal" from both the fact that the Hours are served with more solemnity than normal, commemorating Christ the King who humbled himself for the salvation of mankind, and also from the fact that this service was in the past attended by the Emperor and his court.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vespers_of_Holy_and_Great_Friday">Vespers of Holy and Great Friday</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Vespers of Holy and Great Friday">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg/220px-Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg/330px-Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg/440px-Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2494" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toronto-Apokathylosis-2012-04-13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The crucified Christ, just before the <a href="/wiki/Deposition_from_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Deposition from the Cross">Deposition from the Cross</a> and the placing of the <a href="/wiki/Epitaphios_(liturgical)" title="Epitaphios (liturgical)">Epitaphios</a> in the Sepulcher.</div></div></div><p>
In the afternoon, around 3&#160;pm, all gather for the <i><b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BTqiy-p7EkA">Vespers of the Taking-Down from the Cross</a></b></i>, commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Deposition_from_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Deposition from the Cross">Deposition from the Cross</a>. The Gospel reading is a <a href="/wiki/Concatenation" title="Concatenation">concatenation</a> taken from all four of the Gospels. During the service, the body of Christ (the <i>soma</i>) is removed from the cross, as the words in the Gospel reading mention <a href="/wiki/Joseph_of_Arimathea" title="Joseph of Arimathea">Joseph of Arimathea</a>, wrapped in a linen shroud, and taken to the <a href="/wiki/Altar" title="Altar">altar</a> in the sanctuary.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gold_embroidery_example.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Gold_embroidery_example.jpg/220px-Gold_embroidery_example.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Gold_embroidery_example.jpg/330px-Gold_embroidery_example.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Gold_embroidery_example.jpg/440px-Gold_embroidery_example.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="569" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gold_embroidery_example.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Epitaphios_(liturgical)" title="Epitaphios (liturgical)">epitaphios</a> ("winding sheet"), depicting the preparation of the body of Jesus for burial</div></div></div><p> Near the end of the service an <i><a href="/wiki/Epitaphios_(liturgical)" title="Epitaphios (liturgical)">epitaphios</a></i> or "winding sheet" (a cloth embroidered with the image of Christ prepared for burial) is carried in procession to a low table in the <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> which represents the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Sepulchre" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Sepulchre">Tomb of Christ</a>; it is often decorated with an abundance of flowers. The epitaphios itself represents the body of Jesus wrapped in a burial shroud, and is a roughly full-size cloth icon of the body of Christ. Then the priest may deliver a <a href="/wiki/Homily" title="Homily">homily</a> and everyone comes forward to venerate the epitaphios. In the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> practice, at the end of Vespers, <a href="/wiki/Compline" title="Compline">Compline</a> is immediately served, featuring a special <i>Canon of the Crucifixion of our Lord and the Lamentation of the Most Holy <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a></i> by Symeon the Logothete.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Matins_of_Holy_and_Great_Saturday">Matins of Holy and Great Saturday</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Matins of Holy and Great Saturday">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg/220px-Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg/330px-Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg/440px-Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Epitaphios_Peleka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Epitaphios being carried in <a href="/wiki/Procession" title="Procession">procession</a> in a church in Greece.</div></div></div>
<p>On Friday night, the Matins of <a href="/wiki/Holy_and_Great_Saturday" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy and Great Saturday">Holy and Great Saturday</a>, a unique service known as <i><b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z2_zMVTcdpg&amp;feature=youtu.be">The Lamentation at the Tomb</a></b></i> (<i>EpitÃ¡phios ThrÄnos</i>) is celebrated. This service is also sometimes called <i>Jerusalem Matins</i>. Much of the service takes place around the tomb of Christ in the center of the nave.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>A unique feature of the service is the chanting of the Lamentations or Praises (<i><a href="/wiki/Encomium" title="Encomium">EnkÅmia</a></i>), which consist of verses chanted by the clergy interspersed between the verses of <a href="/wiki/Psalm_119" title="Psalm 119">Psalm 119</a> (which is, by far, the longest <a href="/wiki/Psalm" class="mw-redirect" title="Psalm">psalm</a> in the Bible). The <i>EnkÅmia</i> are the best-loved hymns of Byzantine hymnography, both their poetry and their music being uniquely suited to each other and to the spirit of the day. They consist of 185 <a href="/wiki/Tercet" title="Tercet">tercet</a> <a href="/wiki/Antiphon" title="Antiphon">antiphons</a> arranged in three parts (<i>stÃ¡seis</i> or "stops"), which are interjected with the verses of Psalm 119, and nine short <i>doxastikÃ¡</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Gloria_in_excelsis_Deo" title="Gloria in excelsis Deo">Gloriae</a>") and <i>TheotÃ³kia</i> (invocations to the Virgin Mary). The three <i>stÃ¡seis</i> are each set to its own music, and are commonly known by their initial antiphons: <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">á¼© Î¶Ïá½´ á¼Î½ ÏÎ¬Ïá¿³</span>, "Life in a grave", <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">á¼Î¾Î¹Î¿Î½ á¼ÏÏÎ¯</span>, "Worthy it is", and <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Îá¼± Î³ÎµÎ½ÎµÎ±á½¶ Ïá¾¶ÏÎ±Î¹</span>, "All the generations".  Musically they can be classified as <a href="/wiki/Strophic" class="mw-redirect" title="Strophic">strophic</a>, with 75, 62, and 48 tercet <a href="/wiki/Stanza" title="Stanza">stanzas</a> each, respectively. The climax of the <i>EnkÅmia</i> comes during the third <i>stÃ¡sis</i>, with the antiphon "<i>Å glykÃ½ mou Ãar</i>", a lamentation of the Virgin for her dead Child ("O, my sweet spring, my sweetest child, where has your beauty gone?"). The author(s) and date of the <i>EnkÅmia</i> are unknown. Their High Attic linguistic style suggests a dating around the 6th century, possibly before the time of <a href="/wiki/St._Romanos_the_Melodist" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Romanos the Melodist">St. Romanos the Melodist</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg/220px-Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg/330px-Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg/440px-Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1984" data-file-height="1488" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Epitaph_Adelaide.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Epitaphios mounted upon return of procession, at an Orthodox Church in Adelaide, Australia.</div></div></div>
<p>At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Doxology" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Doxology">Great Doxology</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Trisagion" title="Trisagion">Trisagion</a> is sung, the epitaphios is taken in <a href="/wiki/Crucession" class="mw-redirect" title="Crucession">procession</a> around the outside the church, and is then returned to the tomb. Some churches observe the practice of holding the epitaphios at the door, above waist level, so the faithful most bow down under it as they come back into the church, symbolizing their entering into the death and resurrection of Christ. The epitaphios will lay in the tomb until the Paschal Service early Sunday morning. In some churches, the epitaphios is never left alone, but is accompanied 24 hours a day by a reader chanting from the Psalter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Troparion" title="Troparion">Troparion</a> (hymn of the day) of Good Friday is:
</p>
<blockquote><div class="poem">
<p>The noble <a href="/wiki/Joseph_of_Arimathea" title="Joseph of Arimathea">Joseph</a>, when he had taken down Thy most pure Body from the <a href="/wiki/Tree_of_Life_(Judeo-Christian)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tree of Life (Judeo-Christian)">tree</a>, wrapped it in fine linen, and anointed it with spices, and placed it in a new tomb.<br />
Glory to the <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">Father</a>, and to the <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Son</a>, and to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit" title="Holy Spirit">Holy Spirit</a>, both now and ever, and unto ages of ages. Amen.<br />
The angel came to the <a href="/wiki/Myrrh-bearing_women" class="mw-redirect" title="Myrrh-bearing women">myrrh-bearing women</a> at the tomb and said:<br />
<a href="/wiki/Myrrh" title="Myrrh">Myrrh</a> is fitting for the dead, but Christ has shown Himself a stranger to corruption.
</p>
</div></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_Roman_Catholic_Church">In the Roman Catholic Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: In the Roman Catholic Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_of_Fasting">Day of Fasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Day of Fasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG/220px-St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG/330px-St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG/440px-St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St.Martin-Karfreitag36.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">Crucifix</a> prepared for veneration</div></div></div>
<p>The Catholic Church regards Good Friday and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Saturday" title="Holy Saturday">Holy Saturday</a> as the Paschal fast, in accord with Article 110 of <a href="/wiki/Sacrosanctum_Concilium" title="Sacrosanctum Concilium">Sacrosanctum Concilium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vatican.va_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vatican.va-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin Church</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fasting_and_abstinence_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Fasting and abstinence in the Catholic Church">fast day</a> is understood as having only one full meal and two <a href="/wiki/Collation_(meal)" title="Collation (meal)">collations</a> (a smaller repast, the two of which together do not equal the one full meal)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> â although this may be observed less stringently on Holy Saturday than on Good Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-vatican.va_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vatican.va-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_on_the_day">Services on the day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Services on the day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Rite" title="Roman Rite">Roman Rite</a> has no celebration of <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Lord's Supper</a> on <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">Holy Thursday</a> evening and the <a href="/wiki/Easter_Vigil" title="Easter Vigil">Easter Vigil</a> unless a special exemption is granted for rare solemn or grave occasions by the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_(officer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinary (officer)">local bishop</a>. The only <a href="/wiki/Sacrament" title="Sacrament">sacraments</a> celebrated during this time are <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">Baptism</a> (for those in danger of death), <a href="/wiki/Sacrament_of_Penance_(Catholic_Church)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacrament of Penance (Catholic Church)">Penance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anointing_of_the_Sick" class="mw-redirect" title="Anointing of the Sick">Anointing of the Sick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> While there is no celebration of the Eucharist, it is distributed to the faithful only in the Service of the Passion of the Lord, but can also be taken at any hour to the sick who are unable to attend this service.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> After the Lord's Supper any candlesticks and <a href="/wiki/Altar_cloth" title="Altar cloth">altar cloths</a>, cross or crosses are removed leaving it bare so that they may be returned in-ceremony on Easter Sunday which memorialises the day of Christ's resurrection.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It is also customary to empty the <a href="/wiki/Holy_water" title="Holy water">holy water</a> <a href="/wiki/Holy_water_font" title="Holy water font">fonts</a> in preparation of the blessing of the water at the Easter Vigil.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally, no bells are rung on Good Friday or Holy Saturday until the <a href="/wiki/Easter_Vigil" title="Easter Vigil">Easter Vigil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Celebration of the Passion of the Lord takes place in the afternoon, ideally at three o'clock; however, for pastoral reasons (especially in countries where Good Friday is not a public holiday), it is permissible to celebrate the liturgy earlier, even shortly after midday, or at a later hour up until 9pm.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The vestments used are <a href="/wiki/Liturgical_colours" title="Liturgical colours">red (more commonly) or black (more traditionally)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Before 1970, vestments were black except for the Communion part of the rite when violet was used.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Before 1955 black was used throughout.<sup id="cite_ref-sanctamissa.org_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sanctamissa.org-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> If a bishop or <a href="/wiki/Abbot" title="Abbot">abbot</a> celebrates, he wears a plain <a href="/wiki/Mitre" title="Mitre">mitre</a> (<i>mitra simplex</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Three_Hours.27_Agony"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_Hours'_Agony">Three Hours' Agony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Three Hours&#039; Agony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Three_Hours%27_Agony" title="Three Hours&#39; Agony">Three Hours' Agony</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Three_Hours%27_Agony" title="Three Hours&#39; Agony">Three Hours' Devotion</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Last_Words_from_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven Last Words from the Cross">Seven Last Words from the Cross</a> begins at noon and ends at 3 pm, the time that the Christian tradition teaches that Jesus died on the cross.<sup id="cite_ref-Barron2019_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barron2019-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liturgy">Liturgy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Liturgy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_prayer_for_the_Jews" title="Good Friday prayer for the Jews">Good Friday prayer for the Jews</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ecce_Mass,_Good_Friday,_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes,_Philadelphia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Ecce_Mass%2C_Good_Friday%2C_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/220px-Ecce_Mass%2C_Good_Friday%2C_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes%2C_Philadelphia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Ecce_Mass%2C_Good_Friday%2C_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/330px-Ecce_Mass%2C_Good_Friday%2C_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes%2C_Philadelphia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Ecce_Mass%2C_Good_Friday%2C_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/440px-Ecce_Mass%2C_Good_Friday%2C_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes%2C_Philadelphia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ecce_Mass,_Good_Friday,_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes,_Philadelphia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Communion from the <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Sacrament" title="Blessed Sacrament">Blessed Sacrament</a> on Good Friday (Our Lady of Lourdes, Philadelphia)</div></div></div>
<p>The Good Friday liturgy consists of three parts: the <a href="/wiki/Liturgy_of_the_Word" class="mw-redirect" title="Liturgy of the Word">Liturgy of the Word</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Veneration_of_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Veneration of the Cross">Veneration of the Cross</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Communion" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Communion">Holy Communion</a>.
</p>
<ul><li>The <b>Liturgy of the Word</b> consists of the clergy and assisting ministers entering in complete silence, without any singing. They then silently make a full <a href="/wiki/Prostration" title="Prostration">prostration</a>. This signifies the abasement (<a href="/wiki/Fall_of_man" title="Fall of man">the fall</a>) of (earthly) humans.<sup id="cite_ref-Pope_Francis_prostrating_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pope_Francis_prostrating-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> It also symbolizes the grief and sorrow of the Church.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Then follows the <a href="/wiki/Collect" title="Collect">Collect</a> prayer, and the reading or chanting of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Isaiah+52:13â53:12&amp;version=nrsv">Isaiah 52:13â53:12</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Hebrews+4:14â4:16&amp;version=nrsv">Hebrews 4:14â16</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Hebrews+5:7â5:9&amp;version=nrsv">5:7â9</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Passion_(Christianity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Passion (Christianity)">Passion</a> account from the <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_John" title="Gospel of John">Gospel of John</a>, traditionally divided between three deacons,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> yet usually divided between the celebrant, one or two singers or readers, and the congregation which speaks the part of the "crowd". This part of the liturgy concludes with the <i>orationes sollemnes</i>, a series of prayers for the Church, the Pope, the clergy and laity of the Church, those preparing for baptism, the unity of Christians, the Jewish people, those who do not believe in Christ, those who do not believe in God, those in public office, those in special need.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> After each prayer intention, the deacon calls the faithful to kneel for a short period of private prayer; the celebrant then sums up the prayer intention with a Collect-style prayer.</li>
<li>The <b>Adoration of the Cross</b> has a <a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">crucifix</a>, not necessarily the one that is normally on or near the altar at other times of the year, solemnly unveiled and displayed to the congregation, and then venerated by them, individually if possible and usually by kissing the wood of the cross, while hymns and the <a href="/wiki/Improperia" title="Improperia">Improperia</a> ("Reproaches") with the <a href="/wiki/Trisagion" title="Trisagion">Trisagion</a> hymn are chanted.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Holy Communion</b> is done according to a rite based on that of the final part of Mass, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord&#39;s Prayer">Our Father</a>, but omitting the ceremony of "<a href="/wiki/Fraction_(religion)" title="Fraction (religion)">Breaking of the Bread</a>" and its related chant, the "<a href="/wiki/Agnus_Dei_(liturgy)" title="Agnus Dei (liturgy)">Agnus Dei</a>". The <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Eucharist</a>, consecrated at the Evening Mass of the Lord's Supper on <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">Holy Thursday</a>, is distributed at this service.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Before the reform of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a>, only the priest received Communion in the framework of what was called the "<a href="/wiki/Mass_of_the_Presanctified" title="Mass of the Presanctified">Mass of the Presanctified</a>", which included the usual Offertory prayers, with the placing of wine in the chalice, but which omitted the <a href="/wiki/Canon_of_the_Mass" title="Canon of the Mass">Canon of the Mass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sanctamissa.org_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sanctamissa.org-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The priest and people then depart in silence, and the altar cloth is removed, leaving the altar bare except for the crucifix and two or four candlesticks.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations_of_the_Cross">Stations of the Cross</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Stations of the Cross">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg/170px-GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg/255px-GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg/340px-GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Way_of_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Way of the Cross">Way of the Cross</a>, celebrated at the <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a> in Rome on Good Friday</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG/220px-Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG/330px-Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG/440px-Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rome: canopy erected at the "Temple of Venus and Rome" during the "Way of the Cross" ceremony</div></div></div>
<p>In addition to the prescribed <a href="/wiki/Liturgy" title="Liturgy">liturgical</a> service, the <a href="/wiki/Stations_of_the_Cross" title="Stations of the Cross">Stations of the Cross</a> are often prayed either in the church or outside, and a prayer service may be held from midday to 3.00&#160;pm, known as the <a href="/wiki/Three_Hours%27_Agony" title="Three Hours&#39; Agony">Three Hours' Agony</a>. In countries such as Malta, Italy, Philippines, Puerto Rico and Spain, processions with statues representing the Passion of Christ are held.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In Rome, since the papacy of Saint <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_II" class="mw-redirect" title="John Paul II">John Paul II</a>, the heights of the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Venus_and_Roma" title="Temple of Venus and Roma">Temple of Venus and Roma</a> and their position opposite the main entrance to the Colosseum have been used to good effect as a public address platform. This may be seen in the photograph below where a red canopy has been erected to shelter the Pope as well as an illuminated cross, on the occasion of the <b>Way of the Cross</b> ceremony. The Pope, either personally or through a representative, leads the faithful through meditations on the stations of the cross while a cross is carried from there to the Colosseum.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In Polish churches, a tableau of Christ's Tomb is unveiled in the sanctuary. Many of the faithful spend long hours into the night grieving at the Tomb, where it is customary to kiss the wounds on the Lord's body. A life-size figure of Jesus lying in his tomb is widely visited by the faithful, especially on Holy Saturday. The tableaux may include flowers, candles, figures of angels standing watch, and the three crosses atop Mt Calvary, and much more. Each parish strives to come up with the most artistically and religiously evocative arrangement in which the Blessed Sacrament, draped in a filmy veil, is prominently displayed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acts_of_Reparation_to_Jesus_Christ">Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation_to_Jesus_Christ" title="Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ">Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg/170px-Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg/255px-Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg/340px-Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1737" data-file-height="2429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a>'s <i>Jesus Carrying the Cross</i>, 1580</div></div></div>
<p>The Roman Catholic tradition includes specific prayers and devotions as <i><a href="/wiki/Acts_of_reparation" title="Acts of reparation">acts of reparation</a></i> for the sufferings and insults that Jesus suffered during his Passion on Good Friday. These Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ do not involve a petition for a beneficiary, but aim to "repair the sins" against Jesus. Some such prayers are provided in the <a href="/wiki/Raccolta" title="Raccolta">Raccolta</a> Catholic prayer book (approved by a Decree of 1854, and published by the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> in 1898) which also includes prayers as <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation_to_the_Virgin_Mary" title="Acts of Reparation to the Virgin Mary">Acts of Reparation to the Virgin Mary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his encyclical <i><a href="/wiki/Miserentissimus_Redemptor" title="Miserentissimus Redemptor">Miserentissimus Redemptor</a></i> on reparations, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pope Pius XI</a> called Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ a duty for Catholics and referred to them as "some sort of compensation to be rendered for the injury" with respect to the sufferings of Jesus.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> referred to <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Reparation">Acts of Reparation</a> as the "unceasing effort to stand beside the endless crosses on which the Son of God continues to be crucified".<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novena_to_the_Divine_Mercy">Novena to the Divine Mercy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Novena to the Divine Mercy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Novena" title="Novena">Novena</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Divine_Mercy" title="Divine Mercy">Divine Mercy</a> begins on that day and lasts until the Saturday before <a href="/wiki/Divine_Mercy_Sunday" title="Divine Mercy Sunday">the Feast of Mercy</a>. Both holidays are strictly connected, as the <a href="/wiki/Mercy" title="Mercy">mercy</a> of <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a> flows from the <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart" title="Sacred Heart">Heart of Jesus</a> that was pierced on the <a href="/wiki/Cross" title="Cross">Cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglican_Communion">Anglican Communion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Anglican Communion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 1662 <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Common_Prayer" title="Book of Common Prayer">Book of Common Prayer</a> did not specify a particular rite to be observed on Good Friday but local custom came to mandate an assortment of services, including the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Last_Words_from_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven Last Words from the Cross">Seven Last Words from the Cross</a> and a three-hour service consisting of <a href="/wiki/Matins" title="Matins">Matins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Ante-communion</a> (using the <a href="/wiki/Reserved_Sacrament" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserved Sacrament">Reserved Sacrament</a> in <a href="/wiki/High_church" title="High church">high church</a> parishes) and <a href="/wiki/Evening_Prayer_(Book_of_Common_Prayer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Evening Prayer (Book of Common Prayer)">Evensong</a>. In recent times,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous.
